Yousheng Group's Mount Lu Tour

The Yousheng Travel Agency on Niuzhuang Road considers the scenery of Mount Lu to be the best in Southeast China. Therefore, it has exclusively chartered the entire first-class cabin of the Changxing steamship from the Sanbei Company for a round trip. The tour will depart from Shanghai on the morning of the 19th of this month at exactly 2:00 AM and return to Shanghai from on the afternoon of the 4th of the next month at 2:00 PM, with a total of 12 days on the mountain, so that participants can fully enjoy the scenery. There are 30 places available in the first-class cabin (Type A) and 30 places in the first-class cabin (Type B). The cost is 110 yuan per person for Type A and 95 yuan for Type B, including round-trip tickets, Western meals on the ship, round-trip bus tickets from Jiujiang to Lianhua Cave, mountain sedan chairs up and down the mountain, and mountain accommodation and meals. The agency has advertised the tour and is accepting registrations with tour certificates starting today. It is reported that the number of people registering has been very enthusiastic.

Chinese Seamen's Club, Representatives' Congress Elects Directors

The Chinese Seamen's Special Party Department, the Chinese Seamen's Union, and other organizations jointly launched the Chinese Seamen's Club. Yesterday morning at 9:00 AM, the first plenary session of representatives was held in the auditorium of the Seamen's Party Department. The following were in attendance: Party Department representatives Shen Qi Han, Liu Huo Gong, Hu Qi; Union representatives Cheng Deyuan, Yin Xuzai, Du Jiabao; China Yangtze River Pilots Association representative Feng Fucheng; China Merchants Bureau Cargo Handling Office representative Ma Zhongxian; Commercial Ship Lianyi Association representative Tang Hesheng; Shunying Tongxing Association representative Chen Changshou; Middle Cabin Office representatives Wang Oumin, Xu Jinsan, Zheng Ziqing; Little Yangtze River Club representative Wang Wenhua; Beijun'an Office representative Chen Shaofu; Foreign Port Cargo Handler Mutual Aid Society representative Xu Houzhi; Shunying General Office representative Yang Ruisheng; Shunying South Office representative Sun Tingfu; Sanbei Hong'an Cargo Handling Mutual Aid Society representative Zhang Binghua; New Taikoo Cargo Handling Club representative Qian Zhigang; Nanjun'an Sailors Mutual Aid Association representative Li Wenbao; Jardine Cargo Handling Club representative Zhao Nanshan; Jardine Aft Cabin Tongyi Association representative Wang Shanqing; Navigation Lianyihui representative He Luqiu; Helmsman Carpenter Association representative Kang Jimin; Shanghai Branch of the Seamen's Food and Drink Association representatives Mao Yufeng, Cheng Yongming, Wang Shoru; Shanghai District Party Department representatives Wang Zhida, Zhang Yuchen; and instructors Chen Jun, Xian Xie, Zhou Mugu, Zhang Donglin, Leng Renyi, Zhou Lian, Wang Zhonggang, and others, more than 40 people. Shen Qi Han, Secretary-General of the Party Department, was elected as the chairman. After performing the ceremony, the chairman read the resolutions of the preparatory committee and then made a report, saying, "The purpose of our organization of the Chinese Seamen's Club is to improve morality, strengthen the body, increase knowledge, and harmonize the mind, to move from an irregular life to a disciplined one, to improve life, and create the future. This is all stated in the charter, and we will strive to practice it in the future and strive for perfection. We will gradually add public houses, consumer cooperatives, hospitals, nurseries, etc., to seek thorough improvement and development of life and career." (omitted below) The 13 articles of the charter were then adopted, and it was decided that regular expenses would be freely donated by various institutions and organizations. Finally, Hu Qi, Mao Yufeng, Wang Zhonggang, Shen Qi Han, Cheng Yongming, Wang Oumin, Cheng Deyuan, and seven others were elected as directors, and Liu Huo Gong Zhang Donglin, Peng Bowei, Yin Xuzai, Kang Jimin, Wang Jiyi, Xu Houzhi, and seven others were elected as alternate directors. The meeting adjourned at around 12:00 noon.

Representative of the Sino-Foreign Relief Association Welcomed by Overseas Chinese in Los Angeles

The China Sino-Foreign Relief Association, located at 505 Honan Road, previously intended to report on past relief efforts to overseas Chinese in various ports and to elaborate on the essential points of construction for disaster relief, in order to gain sympathy. Taking advantage of Mr. Baker and Mr. Luo Chuanhua's trip to the United States, they were specially commissioned to serve as representatives to carry out publicity. The two gentlemen set off separately and received warm welcomes from overseas Chinese in Japan, Honolulu, and other places along the way. After leaving Honolulu, Mr. Luo arrived at the port of Wenangdeng in the United States on the 9th of last month aboard the mail ship "Mai Luoluo", and then went to Los Angeles, the film production area. The local Consul Mr. Jiang Yisheng went to the port to meet him and provided warm hospitality. He also introduced Mr. Zhao Baoguang, a leader of the overseas Chinese community, to meet and talk with him. Mr. Zhao is the president of the Chinese Charity Federation in the city. He deeply admired Mr. Luo's mission on this trip. The next day, he gathered representatives from all walks of life to hold a meeting to welcome him. Mr. Luo gave a detailed report on the relief work and construction projects over the years. Those who heard it sympathized and were willing to assist. That evening, a banquet was held to welcome him. During the banquet, the guests and hosts had an exceptionally pleasant time and did not disperse until they were satisfied. Mr. Luo stayed in the city for three days and left by train for Chicago on the 12th of this month. It is reported that he will meet with Mr. Baker and then go to various ports in the eastern United States to vigorously promote their cause.

Sanlin School Principal Ding Guanyan Paints to Aid School Construction

The Gymnasium is Solemn and Grand

Since Mr. Ding Guanyan took over as the principal of Sanlin School in Pudong, not only has the school's spirit improved day by day, but also its material construction has yielded results every year. The school has achieved excellent results in establishing a vocational high school, raising funds to build the Wen Yi Library, adding classrooms, and arranging gardens. The school's affairs are thriving, and it has received commendations from provincial and county supervisors. The reporter recently heard that the school is also building a gymnasium. Yesterday, I made a special trip to visit and saw Mr. Ding with his sleeves rolled up, dipping his brush and ink at his desk, creating a large finger painting of a central hall. His enthusiasm was overflowing, and his artistic conception was vivid. Mr. Ding had studied under Xie Gongzhan of Dantu and Chen Jia of Yushan, and was a disciple of Mr. Lu Lianfu. His finger paintings have opened up new paths, swiftly entering the realm of the ancients. Because he usually paints for leisure, he never takes payment. Therefore, those who know him regard obtaining even a small piece of his work as a treasure. However, Mr. Ding has always been busy with school affairs, and the requests for paintings have accumulated, leaving him no time to sort them out. Therefore, some people have not been able to obtain his paintings for several years. It is said that now, because the school's gymnasium is about to be completed and is heavily in debt, and future equipment is also quite lacking, he intends to make a vow to create one hundred paintings starting from now, with a price of fifteen yuan per four-foot central hall, including mounting, and twenty yuan per five-foot central hall, including mounting. He will issue pre-sale tickets, painting after payment, and all proceeds will be used to help equip the gymnasium. Buyers will also have their names engraved in stone to achieve immortality. It is believed that local people, who are enthusiastic about education, will not only help with construction but also obtain famous paintings and leave their names for posterity, achieving three goals in one stroke, and will definitely be happy to support him. Later, Principal Ding also led a tour of the gymnasium. The scale is grand, magnificent, and beautiful. It is currently under construction and will be completed soon. It has a total of seven buildings, divided into upper, middle, and lower three floors, with a total area of 3,640 square feet. The lower floor has a standard basketball court, a lecture platform, changing rooms, equipment rooms, etc. The middle floor is a grandstand that can accommodate more than 400 spectators. The upper floor is a student dormitory. It requires a total of 15,600 yuan. In addition to the 2,000 yuan donated by Mr. Kang Xitao from this town and more than 1,000 yuan donated by local people, and the appropriation of construction funds from previous years, there is still a shortfall of more than 10,000 yuan, all of which is the school's debt. Therefore, they sincerely hope that the local community will provide more support to make the facilities more perfect.

Engagement of Li Sun: Mr. Li Shuqing and Ms. Sun Yuanzhen held their engagement ceremony at the Great Eastern Restaurant the day before yesterday. The introducers were Mr. Lu Daquan and Mr. Yang Zhixin, and Mr. Pan Guangdan was invited as the witness. Western Clothing Industry Chalk Competition: The Western Clothing Industry Association, in order to cultivate specialized technical talents in the western clothing industry and develop business, established the Western Clothing Industry Vocational Morning School in the spring of this year, with Xia Xiaoqing, the association's supervisor, as the principal, and Gu Hongfa, the standing committee member, as the director of studies. Although it has only been half a year, the results have been remarkable. Yesterday, the association held a chalk competition for the students. The students used the drawing of woolen fabrics as the standard for the competition results. At the same time, the association invited Xu Shanchang, chairman of the Shanghai Municipal Northern Business Association, and Wang Hesheng and Chen Youchang, who are knowledgeable in clothing manufacturing, to serve as judges. As a result, Zhang Linfu won the first place, Sheng Mingshan won the second place, and Fang Jifa won the third place, each receiving a silver shield and a certificate of award. Shi Zhicheng, Shao Guangda, Chen Deli, Wang Maogu, and others also received certificates of award. It is reported that recently, there has been a surge of people from the industry requesting to enroll in the association's morning school.

Efficacy of Zhongfa Rendan: The Longhu brand Rendan sold by the Zhongfa Pharmacy is effective for symptoms such as indigestion, drunkenness, heatstroke, and cold. Therefore, whether at home or traveling, it should be prepared for emergencies. Especially in summer, it should not be forgotten when eating and resting.

Continental Bank Club News: In order to promote proper recreational activities for its employees, the Continental Bank has ordered its branches to organize staff clubs. The Jing'an Temple Road branch took the lead in planning and organizing a committee, electing Zha Hengzhi as honorary chairman, Zheng Rongzeng as chairman, Ye Shisan as design and document committee member, Wang Dongsheng as library committee member, Yuan Yuanfu as accounting committee member, and Ding Youzhu as general affairs committee member. Weather Report

The Zikawei Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the Shandong area, the upper and middle reaches of the Yellow River, and the upper and middle reaches of the Yangtze River would be cloudy and sunny with hot weather and southeast to southwest winds. The wind direction in the lower reaches of the Yangtze River is uncertain, with local thunderstorms. The East China Sea is sunny and clear with a gentle southeast wind. The weather around Taiwan is uncertain. The hurricane northwest of Palau Island will continue to move northwest. Its center was within 120 miles of 12 degrees north latitude and 134 degrees east longitude at 2:00 PM. The wind force is unknown. Also, in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in Shanghai was 95.7 degrees and the lowest was 77.4 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest was 85.5 degrees and the lowest was 74.7 degrees.

11th Olympic Games

World Games Basketball Qualifying Tournament: Our Team Defeats France Yesterday; American Team Maintains 40 Seconds in the 400-Meter Relay; World Record in Women's 100-Meter Freestyle

Berlin Electric: At 5:00 PM on the 8th of the Games, the Sino-French basketball qualifying tournament was held, resulting in a score of 45 to 38, with China winning. (Central News Agency Correspondent's Telegram on the 8th)

(Berlin) The World Games swimming competition was held here this morning. The preliminary results are sufficient to prove that the swimming championship will be contested by the United States and Japan. In the past four years, both countries' teams have made unparalleled progress. (National News Agency Telegram on the 8th)

Central News Agency World Games Correspondent's Berlin Broadcast: The track and field championships of the World Games are held separately for each event. In the men's category, the United States won 8 championships, Germany 3, Finland 2, and the United Kingdom, Japan, and New Zealand 1 each. In the women's category, Germany 2, the United States 1, and Italy 1. In the ball games, Norway won against Germany 2-0, and Italy won against Japan 8-0 today. Basketball has entered the second round. The results of the past games are as follows: Estonia beat France 34-29, Chile beat Turkey 30-16, Switzerland beat Germany 25-18, Czechoslovakia beat Hungary 2-0, Egypt beat Peru 35-22, Latvia beat Uruguay 20-17, Canada beat Brazil 24-17, Italy beat Poland 44-29, and Mexico beat Belgium 32-9. Japan beat China 35-19. During the Sino-Japanese basketball game yesterday, our overseas Chinese and students in Europe paid close attention. About 4,500 to 4,600 overseas Chinese went to watch and organized cheering squads to cheer and support, creating a strong atmosphere. Before the game, our team members all thought they could win. However, the Japanese spirit of hard work is truly admirable. Recalling the Far Eastern Games, it was common for our basketball team to overcome Japan. Now that we have received this lesson, we should strive forward and practice diligently in the future. During the game, our forwards were still active, taking advantage of opportunities. However, the poor shooting accuracy and missed free throws were the main reasons for the failure. The team members were too eager to win, which inevitably led to chaos, resulting in inaccurate shooting. According to statistics, our country had 16 free throws, but only made 2. Japan had 17 free throws against us, making 15. The ratio is very far apart, and the focus of the loss is also here. In other shooting aspects, the Japanese team is not superior to us. I hope our countrymen will learn from this lesson and work hard in training. This afternoon, we will have a simple elimination match against the French team.

Records of Accompanying the World Games Delegation (Letter 7) Special Correspondent Feng Youzhen from the Central News Agency

Cairo Museum

At half-past eight, a guide took us to an ancient palace, the palace of the 12th-century Sultan Saladin. Due to its age and repeated troop deployments, some of the buildings had already collapsed. The palace was built on top of a small hill, commanding a high position and overlooking the entire city. It is now occupied by the British army and has been converted into a fortress. As we walked to the top of the hill, the sound of military bugles filled the ancient palace with an aura of ferocity.

The architecture of the palace is naturally magnificent. Although it has been repeatedly ravaged by war, the remaining parts have been cleaned up and are still very tidy. The guide led us to the back of the palace, and looking out, we had a panoramic view of the entire city, further highlighting the importance of the small hill's terrain. He gave me a brief explanation of the situation in Cairo. To the left is the area where Muslims live. It is said that according to Islamic customs, after people die and are buried underground, houses are built on top of them, so Cairo can be said to be a city where the living and the dead live together. To the right is the area where white people live, with tall and orderly buildings and shady trees, the scenery is quite beautiful. A very long aqueduct has been built along the Nile River, and all the water used by the city is drawn in through this aqueduct. The bottom of the aqueduct is made into semi-circular wide holes, just like a long bridge, which is quite spectacular. To the right of the palace is a mosque, a relic of the 15th century, with a huge dome that fully expresses a solemn atmosphere. After enjoying the panoramic view of Cairo from the back of the palace, we hurried to the museum at half-past nine.

The Egyptian Museum was built in 1900 and is only thirty-six years old. Inside, it is filled with antiquities related to Egyptian culture. Before this museum was built, these antiquities were kept in the old museum. The new museum has magnificent architecture and is a one-story building. Our first impression when we walked in was that the order was very good. We didn't see any police or guards at the entrance, but Egypt has never had any cases of theft or loss of antiquities. The Egyptians have truly regarded these antiquities as national treasures, as the crystallization of national culture, and no one harbors selfish intentions to take them as personal treasures. Everyone who enters to visit must first buy a ticket, five piastres (about one shilling) per person, and enter in order from a revolving door. All the antiquities are displayed in an orderly manner, so that visitors can appreciate them in a very systematic way.

Our guide is a Jew who is well-versed in the history of Egyptian culture. His name is Charles Coldhabar. He has lived in Egypt for thirty years, speaks twelve languages, and explains the important antiquities in detail, endlessly, with a dry tongue and chapped lips, and sometimes with a humorous tone, which makes us laugh.

The antiquities displayed in the museum range from the pre-dynastic period of Egypt to the last dynasty (the Thirtieth Dynasty), and can be said to have been collected without omission. If you want to do a detailed study, you have to ask an archaeological expert to spend several years or even decades. We only took an hour to take a quick look, so of course we can't talk about any insights. I can only give the readers a brief introduction based on the most important antiquities that the guide explained to us.

The museum downstairs displays many stone statues of Egyptian emperors, various idols, and stone coffins of emperors. These are all relics from thousands of years ago. The carvings are extremely exquisite and show the beauty of ancient Egyptian art, which is worthy of being the originator of Western culture.

What attracted our attention the most was the gold coffin and mummy of Tutankhamun displayed upstairs. Tutankhamun was the king of the Eighteenth Dynasty of Egypt, around 1555 BC. His gold coffin and mummy were excavated from his pyramid by British archaeologist Dr. Howard Carter with the permission of the Egyptian government. It was in 1922, only fourteen years ago. At that time, newspapers around the world published many detailed texts and photos about the excavation process and its results, which can be said to have caused a sensation. It is said that when the emperors of Egypt died, they all carried a curse: whoever went to excavate his tomb would not die well. It is said that the workers who participated in this excavation did not end well, and Dr. Carter also went mad and committed suicide for no reason. Whether such a legend is far-fetched or not, the reporter is not an archaeologist and does not need to verify it. However, his excavation of this ancient tomb has made a great contribution to the history of Egyptian culture, which is beyond doubt. Tutankhamun's coffin is three-dimensional in shape, with a door on each layer and a hidden lock on it. The outside of the gold coffin is inlaid with many jewels and carved with many patterns. It is truly exquisite. The outermost layer is about fifteen feet wide, and the other layers are smaller than each other. They were originally nested inside, but now they are displayed separately in large glass cabinets. A total of 225 kilograms of gold were used, one small piece of which is now found to contain copper. The guide said humorously, perhaps the workers at the time were embezzling. Tutankhamun's tomb is not the largest one in the pyramids. If the tombs of Danbos or Chephren were excavated, the greatness of their gold coffins would be even more amazing.

The emperors of Egypt believed in eternal life, so after they died, they applied specially made spices to their bodies, which could never rot. Only the heart could not be preserved, so it was dug out after death and replaced with a stone heart. These corpses are called mummies and have indeed been preserved for thousands of years, still as complete as if they were alive. I think modern scientists and pharmacists will also sigh that they are not as good as the ancient Egyptians who invented this preservative.

The mummy of King Tutankhamun is also displayed in the museum and cannot be visited. This golden body was cast according to the shape of the mummy. Not only are the body, hands, and feet completely in line with the mummy, but also the appearance, eyebrows, and eyes are no different from the real thing. It is lifelike. The golden body is also decorated with many precious patterns, and the craftsmanship is ingenious. Even the works of modern sculptors are far from comparable. There are three layers to the golden body, which are also nested one on top of the other, and then placed in the gold coffin.

Because of their belief in eternal life, the Egyptian emperors not only used preservatives to preserve their bodies, but also brought many treasures into the coffin. The treasures excavated from King Tutankhamun's coffin are all rare and precious, and there are too many to count. The most interesting thing is that the ancient Egyptians not only believed that the emperors were their masters in life and their gods after death, and were willing to serve their emperors for life, but also believed in the theory of eternal life and wanted to take advantage of their emperors' blessings and follow them to eternal life. They could not build pyramids, let alone use preservatives to preserve their bodies, so they came up with the idea of carving their models out of stone and burying them in the emperor's coffin. These stone statues are only a little over a foot long and are also very exquisitely carved. The stupidity of the ancient Egyptians can also be seen.

In addition to Tutankhamun's mummy, the museum also displays two mummies, I don't know which two emperors they are. Both of them are in wooden shells. Not only has the wooden shell not rotted, but one of them has five toes exposed, no different from a person who has just died. In a glass cabinet, there are rows and rows of gemstone rings, estimated to be one or two thousand in total. These were all worn by the emperors of the past, with the names of the emperors engraved on them. All the rings of the Egyptian emperors have been collected inside, without any missing. According to the guide, if anyone were to take a ring away, it would be like tearing a page from the entire history of Egyptian culture. But these rings, displayed in the glass cabinet, will never be missing.

In another glass cabinet is a queen's feather fan, also an antiquity from 3,500 years ago. The feathers are clearly visible, I really don't know what method they used to preserve them. The fan handle is installed horizontally, and when in use, it can be turned into a circle. She can also be said to have thought about the way to enjoy herself very thoughtfully.

There are too many other precious antiquities to see and write about. Due to time constraints, we left the museum at half-past ten with infinite regret and went to the Cairo train station.

Port Said on the Suez Canal

At 11:00 AM, we boarded the train from Cairo to Port Said, bidding farewell to this lovely ancient capital. From Cairo to Port Said is about 200 miles, and both railway and highway are accessible. The railway is double-track and takes four hours to reach. Along the way, except for a very small part that can be cultivated, the rest is a sea of yellow sand. When the train speeds forward, yellow sand and coal ash fly in through the windows, and everyone almost becomes a Negro. The train travels for about an hour and then runs parallel to the Suez Canal. Before we went to Cairo, we thought that if we visited the ancient capital of the birthplace of Western culture, we would not be able to appreciate this great man-made canal. But as a result, we had both fish and bear's paw, and our joy could not be added. Before the Suez Canal was opened, Eurasian traffic had to detour through Africa. Now that the Suez Canal has connected the Mediterranean Sea and the Red Sea, the voyage between Europe and Asia has been shortened by an unknown amount. Such a great project, compared with the Great Wall of China, which was only for defending against the Huns and maintaining personal foundation, its value is incomparable. The Suez Canal was started in 1859 by Ferdinand Delesseps, a Frenchman, and after an unknown amount of hardship, it took ten years to complete in 1869, at a cost of 200 million yuan. It was originally owned by France and Egypt, but later most of the shares were bought by England, and now the power is completely in the hands of England. When the train is running parallel to this great river, we look at the river body, which is full of turquoise water and more than 100 yards wide, not only marveling at the greatness of its engineering, but also feeling its charming tranquility, adding infinitely lovely scenery to the monotonous desert. At 3:00 PM, the train arrived in Port Said, and the mail ship had arrived an hour earlier. Port Said is a city belonging to Egypt, located on the Mediterranean Sea, at the northern end of the Suez Canal, and its location is extremely important. When Leser opened the canal, the British governor of Egypt, Mohommed Said, strongly supported it, so he named this place Port Said (also known as Port Said) to commemorate his achievements. After we got off the train, many people were still interested in touring, so they took cars to tour the city. The reporter was rushing to send a letter, and the post office was very close to the port, so he first took a motorboat back to the ship.

In the places the reporter has been to, the disorder, chaos, cunning, and shamelessness of the people, have probably never been greater than in Port Said. When the reporter returned to the mail ship and landed again, because the motorboat prepared by the company failed to sail on time, he and Mr. Hao Gengsheng hired a commercial motorboat together. The price was clearly stated as one shilling for both of them, but after landing, the boatman insisted on one shilling per person. No matter how you argued, he always defied his conscience, thickened his skin, and refused to admit it. Finally, the reporter asked him to guarantee with his national personality that he was not ripping them off, but he would rather disregard the country's reputation and insisted on this shilling. We didn't have time, and it wasn't worth arguing with him about this small matter, so we could only laugh and accept this ripoff.

According to people who have toured Port Said, no matter where you go, there are always many idlers who ask you to go here and there to buy this and that, and even pull you around and entangle you endlessly. There are many locals on the street who openly sell obscenities, and there are also many who ask you to watch nude dances and erotic films. Everyone can only politely decline. At half-past four, everyone took the company's motorboat and left this filthy city, returning to the mail ship. At half-past five, the ship set sail and exited the mouth of the Suez Canal, continuing forward towards the Mediterranean Sea. Looking back at the great bronze statue of Leser standing on the bank of the Suez Canal, fantasizing about the hardships and difficulties he encountered in opening this great river, I couldn't help but burst into admiration.

Zhejiang Province's Counties and Cities Implement Compulsory Education Plan, Requiring a Total of More Than 630,000 Yuan in Funding

The Ministry of Education previously issued an order informing Zhejiang Province of the 210,000 yuan in funding allocated by the central government for compulsory education in the 25th year of the Republic. The method for the province to raise its own funds has been jointly ordered by the three departments of civil affairs, finance, and education, requiring each county and city to collect the original autonomous household donations together from the 25th year of the Republic, and to add a new slaughter tax as funding for compulsory education. For the implementation of the first phase of compulsory education in various counties and cities of Zhejiang Province in the 25th year of the Republic, the province has planned that Hangzhou City and 75 counties in Zhejiang Province should establish 2,652 short-term primary schools in the first phase of the 25th year. Schools or institutions should attach 2,484 short-term primary school classes, requiring a total of 622,040 yuan in funding, of which 415,622 yuan will be allocated by the central government and the provincial government, and 200,748 yuan will be raised by the counties and cities themselves.

Finance: Morale is Low; Gold Price Continues to Decline

As a result, the price fell by another six jiao, with only a slight difference from the closing price. In the morning, the overseas silver market showed a rise in London and stable prices in the US. The forward silver price in Montry also remained unchanged. Exchange rates also increased. The price of raw gold in London remained unchanged. The Central Bank's listed prices were announced, with both British and American currencies remaining stable. The customs gold unit remained unchanged. The listed price for standard gold bars was still 1126.3 yuan. The off-market preliminary trading opened, and due to the supply from Da De Cheng, the price retreated to within 27 yuan. The morning opened with low prices. After the opening, major players entered the market, and there was a slight rebound. The HSBC's listed prices were announced, with both British and American currencies remaining stable, and the silver balance tax rose by 25. At this point, supply and demand were balanced, and the price struggled around 27.5 yuan. However, sellers easily gained the upper hand, and the price continued to decline. At the same time, Japanese merchants estimated that China's cotton fields had greatly increased, and production had surged, exceeding 15 million dan, which is a huge increase of 5 million dan compared to the Cotton Industry Statistics Association's estimate of 9,596,684 dan last year. This news of a huge harvest made people uneasy, and sellers were active. The new cotton trend felt very sluggish, and short sellers gathered. However, whether there will be any changes in the weather in the future is still questionable. It was found that new cotton was sold to various Chinese and foreign factories, about 23,000 bales of white-packaged cotton, Tongzhou cotton, Taicang cotton, Yao cotton, and Fire Machine, which shows the factory's strong appetite and active procurement. Special Article　Reply to Mr. Hu Yunwen of Yancheng

Cotton called by the piece is calculated at 500 pounds per piece.

Cotton called by the bag is calculated at 120 jin old scale per bag.

Yao flower is only 60 jin old scale per bag.

Wooden frame flower is 150 jin or 200 jin old scale per piece. The packaging of cotton in our country has always been inconsistent, and each type is different. The old scale is 1.21 times the market scale.

The weekly cotton stock statistics in this newspaper only refer to the amount in each warehouse in Shanghai. The factory's flower stock is not included. Most of the flower number goods are mostly used for mortgage exchange.

The total amount of raw cotton needed by all factories in Shanghai, both Chinese and foreign, is 3.52 million dan old scale per year. Currently, some spinning mills have suspended operations due to poor business, and consumption has naturally decreased.

The address where cotton transactions are concentrated is the Cotton Industry Association, and most of the business on Jinlong Street is transacted within the association, and some is transacted in the Yarn and Cloth Exchange.

Regarding books or publications on the yarn and flower business, the Spinning Mill Federation compiled "Textile Times", which is published twice a week, recording domestic cotton industry news and the world cotton industry situation, consumption situation, pricing is very　, 2 yuan per year, postage 5 jiao. Regarding the situation of spinning mills, there is a list of all spinning mills in the country; regarding the situation of cotton production, there are statistics on cotton production in China.

The price values of American cotton and Indian cotton recorded in this newspaper are all converted according to the market catty price. American cotton shipped to Shanghai must be added with tariffs, water feet, and freight, totaling 14.5 yuan per market dan, and Indian cotton is 12 yuan to 13 yuan per market dan.

Indian cotton White Locke cotton is similar to our country's standard flower varieties.

American cotton Middling is the raw material for spinning 32-count fine yarn.

Children's Special

Aim to Do Great Things, Not to Be a High Official

— Yan Maode

Recently, at a friend's house, I heard his mother say to her child: "Now that you have graduated from elementary school and are going to middle school, study hard. In the future, if you become a high official, your parents will be able to live comfortably for the rest of their lives."

Children! Think calmly, is this instilling this outdated thinking into your parents? Because you are instilled with it in your mind every day, developing the habit of wanting to be a high official, you will naturally take being an official as a prerequisite in society, only caring about yourself.

What is meant by great things? It means: "No matter what you do, you must have a beginning and an end, and do it thoroughly and successfully. That is a great thing." In the past, after Watt invented the steam engine, the world's industry underwent a major change, from handicrafts to machine industry. When he invented the steam engine, he saw the steam surging in the kettle and pushing the lid open. He therefore consulted his mother, who gave a vague answer. He was dissatisfied and began to study it, and it took him twenty years to complete the steam engine. Pasteur devoted his energy to investigating things that ordinary people could not see. These tiny things were beyond the reach of ordinary people's eyesight, but Pasteur studied their structure, properties, and relationship to certain things from beginning to end, creating a systematic result, which is microorganisms. Therefore, the world knew that it was necessary to eliminate these microorganisms. Pasteur studied these small things, but he was able to do it thoroughly and achieved results, which became a great thing; therefore, Watt, Pasteur, and others are eternally immortal in history.

This proves that people should set their ambitions when they are young, and they will naturally succeed in the future. Therefore, I hope that all children will first determine their own ambitions and their own outlook on life, so that they can benefit the country and society when they grow up. For thousands of years, there have been many people in China with aspirations, but their ambition to be officials is an outdated idea, focusing on personal development and seeking personal happiness.

Dear children! Always remember: Aim to do great things, not to be a high official.

A Patriotic Child Who Committed Suicide

— Lu Guowei

Children, I am telling you a sad piece of news: In Pucheng, there was a fourteen-year-old child, surnamed Zhou, named Zixin. He usually studied very hard and often went to the library to read books and newspapers. The teachers and students of the school respected him very much. Recently, this respectable child of ours saw that the national situation was becoming more and more critical, and that there was still civil war in his own country. In grief and indignation, he secretly found a bottle of nitric acid and swallowed it to commit suicide. Later, when his family found out and wanted to treat him, it was too late. This respectable and lovable child had left this world and bid us farewell forever.

Children! After seeing this tragic and solemn suicide, what should we feel besides sympathizing with this child? I think this patriotic suicide is indeed a manifestation of patriotic enthusiasm and can awaken some people who are oblivious to national affairs and live in a drunken stupor. However, if all the children in the country follow his example and commit suicide because of patriotism, then who will be responsible for saving the country in the future? Therefore, this is not a positive and rational solution, but a negative and irrational one. The truly positive and rational way to save the country is for children to work hard in their studies from today onwards, cultivate a healthy body and mind, and develop a spirit of mutual assistance and love. Prepare for the time when the country needs us, we can use our rich knowledge and healthy body to serve the country, save the country, and restore the glory of our motherland. At that time, this patriotic child will also smile at us from beyond the grave.

Mosquitoes

— Zhen

The fire-like sun shines its intense light directly onto the ground, so the mercury column on the thermometer has risen to about a hundred degrees. The trees are drooping their heads, looking very frustrated, allowing it to trample them without resistance. People are also fanning themselves and sweating, constantly shouting "hot" - flies and mosquitoes have a good opportunity to be active, searching for their food in groups, working separately. Daytime is the working time for flies, and nighttime is the working time for mosquitoes.

Of course, Min'er's home is also inevitably attacked by mosquitoes at night, and they are in groups, their traces can be found everywhere. Because his home is located in a remote area, and the ponds and green grass are all major bases for mosquito production, the harm from mosquitoes in the summer is not small. Min'er is the most afraid of mosquitoes in his family, so he often takes a cattail fan as a weapon to drive away mosquitoes when enjoying the cool breeze at night. He feels that these mosquitoes are really hateful and always wants to find a way to eliminate them, so he discusses this issue with his older brother, Cong'er: "Brother, how can we eliminate mosquitoes?"

"This is a big question. There are ways to eliminate them, like mosquito coils, but this is not a fundamental method. I think the fundamental method is to kill its eggs and larvae, then mosquitoes will certainly not be found again. Although this is a fundamental method, it must be implemented by everyone in the country, because they can fly, otherwise what is the use?"

"Speaking of mosquitoes, I have a question, that is, I often hear people say that they have malaria. How does this malaria occur? Is it transmitted by mosquitoes?"

"Malaria is originally caused by sporozoa in microorganisms that parasitize the red blood cells in the human body. When anopheles mosquitoes (a type of mosquito that specializes in transmitting malaria) suck the blood of people with malaria, the malaria parasites are sucked into their stomachs along with the blood and undergo very complex developmental changes in their bodies. When these anopheles mosquitoes suck other people's blood again, the malaria parasites are transmitted to those people's bodies along with the saliva of the anopheles mosquitoes, and those people develop malaria. Therefore, we must always pay attention to these anopheles mosquitoes sucking our blood, but how can we distinguish between anopheles mosquitoes and ordinary mosquitoes? Ordinary mosquitoes and anopheles mosquitoes are easy to distinguish: (1) The wings of ordinary mosquitoes are transparent, while the wings of anopheles mosquitoes have brown spots. (2) The head and thorax of ordinary mosquitoes are gray, and the abdomen is slightly green. The entire body of anopheles mosquitoes is yellowish-brown. (3) Ordinary mosquitoes fly with a high-pitched sound, while anopheles mosquitoes fly with a lower sound. (4) Ordinary mosquitoes have a smaller body, while anopheles mosquitoes have a larger body than ordinary mosquitoes. (5) When ordinary mosquitoes are stationary on the wall, their bodies are parallel to the wall surface, and their hind legs are upward. When anopheles mosquitoes are stationary, their bodies are not parallel to the wall surface, and their hind legs droop slightly. (6) The legs of ordinary mosquitoes are slightly longer than their bodies, while the legs of anopheles mosquitoes are twice as long as their bodies. (7) The eggs of ordinary mosquitoes are oval and are often laid in dirty water, with as many as two or three hundred eggs, clustered together. The eggs of anopheles mosquitoes are thin and are often laid in clear water, with only twenty or so eggs, and are not clustered together. (8) The larvae of ordinary mosquitoes (wrigglers) are brown and have longer respiratory tubes, so they droop downward from the water surface when breathing. The wrigglers of anopheles mosquitoes are green and have shorter respiratory tubes, so their bodies are parallel to the water surface when breathing."

The Deer and the Woodcutter

— Lan Shan

One day, a deer was strolling leisurely in the forest when it suddenly heard the sound of someone riding a horse. They were hunters, and that deer was their target.

The deer ran away desperately, but no matter what, it could still hear the hunters chasing after it. It had already walked a very, very long way, and it felt that all four legs were tired. At this time, it happened to meet a woodcutter.

It rushed to the woodcutter, asking with a begging expression:

"Uncle Woodcutter, where can I hide! Alas! Where can I hide my body?"

"Go into my hut!" The woodcutter pointed to his own house and replied, "I will definitely not tell them that you are hiding there!"

So it hid in the hut. And the hunters had already chased after it. They saw the woodcutter and asked him if he had just seen a deer pass by. He did not answer them, but only pointed to the hut with his hand.

But although the deer was hiding in the house, it was constantly watching the woodcutter's actions. Now that it knew the woodcutter had leaked the news, it hurriedly jumped out of the window and left before the hunters came to attack it.

When the hunters saw that the deer had left, they said, "Let it go today! We don't want that deer." With that, they went back.

A few days later, the woodcutter met the deer and asked it with dissatisfaction:

"Why did you leave without thanking me that day?"

It replied, "Because you are not honest - you broke your promise!"

"But I didn't tell those hunters that you were hiding there!"

"Okay," the deer said, "Although you didn't tell them with your tongue and mouth, you used your hand to tell them. The harm of your dishonesty is still the same. - I don't need a friend like you either." After saying that, it left without looking back.

Little Poetry Painting

— Xu Peiying —

— Little Hospital

During summer vacation at home,

Everyone plays the game of medicine;

Older brother is the doctor,

Wearing glasses and a mustache;

Younger sister is the nurse,

With a large white cloth wrapped around her head;

Younger brother is the customer,

Bringing patients to see the doctor;

One, two, three, four.

Oh! The doctor sighs:

There are so many patients,

Now I will heal you all;

Dietary hygiene is the best!

Children's Creations

My Summer Vacation Life

— Feng Huizhen

Time flies so fast, like flowing water, and in a short time, summer vacation has arrived again.

But this vacation is very long. During this month or so, of course, we can't just chat, talk, and play all day long. I think we must do some work. Now I will write down my summer vacation life:

(1) Do holiday homework every day.

(2) Tutor subjects that I failed.

(3) Physical exercise.

(4) Read books that are beneficial outside of school.

(5) Keep a diary every day.

(6) Take a bath every day.

(7) Sometimes tell stories and jokes with my siblings.

(8) Help my parents with housework every day.

Making an Active Film Projector

— Cao Jianpei

Children! This is a very easy scientific trick to do. If you are all willing to try it, I am very willing to join your team and work together.

Find a pair of scissors, a needle and thread, and a piece of cardboard (if there is other beautiful paperboard, that would be even better). Cut the cardboard into two and a half inches high and three and a half inches long. On the cardboard, use colored pencils to draw a goldfish bowl on one side (as shown in Figure 1) and a goldfish on the other side (as shown in Figure 2). Or draw them on white paper and paste them onto the cardboard with paste. After these procedures are completed, use a needle to drill a hole at each end of the cardboard, and tie a string to each hole (as shown in Figure 3). Okay, our film projector is made, and we have an active film to watch.

How to start it? And how to watch it?

Children! Let me tell you. Our active film is not as grand as the ones in movie theaters. There are no ticket sellers, ticket takers, film projectors, or audiences. We are the ones who make and show the films, and we are also the audience. But we don't charge fees, so we don't need ticket sellers or ticket takers. Hold the strings at both ends of the cardboard tightly with your hands, and rotate the two strings alternately with your thumb and index finger, rotating them a little faster. Then look at the cardboard, how is it? Haha! The goldfish are being raised in the goldfish bowl.

Find another piece of cardboard. Draw a bird on one side and a cage on the other side, let's play it again, isn't it interesting, the bird is in the cage.

We can change many patterns according to the above method, such as drawing an athlete kicking a ball, a young teacher teaching, or a strongman shooting an arrow. As long as you can think of it, you can try to draw it on the cardboard as much as possible.

Children, what is the principle behind this? In fact, this is an active film. Originally, the goldfish are on one side of the cardboard, and the goldfish bowl is on the other side of the cardboard. Because the speed of the cardboard rotation blurs our eyeballs, and at the same time, because the speed of the cardboard rotation transforms the shadows of the two sides into one, so when we look at it, the goldfish are being raised in the bowl.

If we make four or five pieces of cardboard, or dozens of pieces of cardboard, in the same way, and draw them in a series of comic strips, it will be like watching a movie scene by scene.

Children! Real active films are also made up of many pictures in succession, reflected by electric light.

Cold Boiled Water

— Fang Zheng

On Sunday, Ming'er came back from the sports field, covered in sweat, and wanted to get some cold water to quench his thirst. His older brother, Zhi'er, saw him and quickly stopped him, saying: "You can't drink cold water. I have some cold boiled water here, take some and drink it!" Ming'er drank the ice-like cold boiled water, but felt very strange. He thought to himself: They are both cold, why can't I drink cold water, but I can drink ice-like cold boiled water? What is the reason for this? So he asked his brother.

"What's the reason? It's a long story, but I can only tell you the main point now. Cold water is raw water, because it has not been cooked by heat, there are many active bacteria (microorganisms) in it. Although we can't see them with our naked eyes, we can see their original form under a microscope. According to the great French scientist Pasteur, every pound of cold water contains as many as 20% bacteria. If we eat bacteria into our stomachs, it will cause changes, such as cholera, abdominal pain, dysentery, etc. Therefore, cold water cannot be drunk lightly. Cold boiled water has been through a heating process, it has become hot water itself, and the bacteria have been killed. This cold is only temporary, but its degree is no different from that of boiling water, so drinking it in summer is not only harmless, but also beneficial!"

Ming'er listened to his brother's words and realized his past mistakes, so from this day on, he corrected them.

The Use of Nose Hair

— Microbe

Children, the "nose hair" in the nose tube grows inside, and it seems to have no use at all. Some people who are idle stick their fingers into the nose tube and pluck a few hairs, thinking that it doesn't matter much anyway, and relieve their loneliness. In fact, everything that is born on the human body must have some use. For example, when a strong wind blows and dust sweeps in, can't the "nose hair" block it and prevent the dust from entering? Usually: When we wash our face every morning, we only need to roll the towel a few times in our nose, and you will be "blackened" on the towel that you won't believe. So if there were no "nose hair", it would definitely be even worse!

Children, "nose hair" is like the "wire" screen window installed on a new-style house, don't pull it out!

Older Brother Fishing by the River

— Lu Yunqian, 12-year-old Female Student

Boy Scout Mailbox

Bamboo Tube Rice

——Reply to Wang Jiasheng, Chinese School, Yokohama, Japan

Brother Jiasheng: You must be a "veteran" of outdoor living, otherwise you wouldn't have written such an interesting letter. I wonder if our guess is correct?

That's right, when we go outdoors, the lighter the supplies, the better. But we have to bring at least some of our cooking utensils, otherwise there will be panic, unless we eat dry food. However, some travelers can solve their eating problems very satisfactorily even if they have nothing with them.

You say you know how to use hot stones to fry eggs, mud to bake chicken, fire ash to roast sweet potatoes, and branches to bake bread, but you don't know if there is any simple way to cook rice. You can't be blamed for this, even though you are already a senior Boy Scout; because few people pay attention to this problem.

But here we have a very wonderful way to tell you, which is to cook rice in a bamboo tube.

You can first find a large bamboo tube. One end must have a bamboo node as the bottom. Then pour in the washed rice, add the appropriate amount of water, and then use washed grass to plug the mouth of the bamboo tube tightly. This completes your work. Then throw it into the fire, after a while, you can hear a louder cracking sound, which is when the bamboo tube splits, then you take it out, and at this time, a tube of hot rice is already in front of you.

It's strange to say, bamboo tubes can also cook rice! This was told to us by a Boy Scout who traveled all over the country, saying that it was a valuable gain from his experience! Japan is also a bamboo-producing area, I hope you can try it out!

Our Boy Scouts originally used everything in nature as our slaves at any time, I hope you will pay more attention to this point and often give us valuable reports! That's all, I wish you success!

Sincerely, China Boy Scout Self-Help Society

The King and the Shepherd Boy (3)

— Xin

The shepherd boy replied, "It is for my father to watch over the flock of sheep. He had it long before I was born."

The little king asked, "How old are you?"

"Yesterday I was exactly seventeen years old"? The shepherd boy replied.

The little king cheered and said, "You are also seven years old? This is so much fun! Yesterday I was also exactly seven years old," but who lives with you? They certainly don't want you to run out here alone, do they?

The shepherd boy replied, "But I had to run out alone, and I really want to go home."

The little king wondered, "You like to go home? This is so much fun! When I am at home, I want to run out; sitting on this silver-like frost! You have been playing with these strangely beautiful sheep for so long? Their bells, how beautiful they are! Where did you get that shepherd's crook? I would really like to get one like that too. Just like yours."

At that time, a tall man bowed low and interjected, "Your Majesty, we must go back. Just now it seemed that the tutor said that Your Majesty's studies are important, and today you can only rest for an hour."

The king stamped his feet and scolded! "Tch! How annoying! I can't stand those tiresome lessons! I must stay outside in the sunshine." Then he asked the shepherd boy, "Child, let me ask you, when do you go back to do your homework?"

The shepherd boy shook his head and said, "I don't do any homework."

The king shouted happily, "What do you mean, you don't do any homework? Hey! You are a lucky child. Then how long will you stay outside?"

The shepherd boy replied, "I won't go back until it gets dark."

The king啧啧 said again, "I won't go back until it gets dark? Hey-hey-hey-hey! How lovely! I never come out in the evening, I really like to watch the stars appear in the sky. Have you ever seen a glittering star pierce through the darkness and come out? Hey! But where are your clothes?"

The shepherd boy hurriedly said, "I don't have any clothes."

The king said in surprise, "So you just wear that dead sheep on your body, that's all? It must be very comfortable. My clothes are hot and heavy."

Shen Bao Local Supplement Amateur Weekly

Life Guidance

How to Satisfy Your Appetite?

— Cao Youmin

Speaking of appetite, everyone can recall the old saying, "Eating, drinking, and sex are the greatest desires of man!" Therefore, if you spend a little effort and time on the study of food in order to satisfy your appetite, it is probably something that fellow enthusiasts would be happy to hear about, right? But I want to remind everyone that this article is not about introducing you to places to buy food and drinks, but rather telling you how to enjoy food prepared by your own hands in a situation where you need to do it yourself. Sometimes, for example, when you are traveling alone and not used to the local cuisine, the same fish, meat, and vegetables can be impossible to swallow. You can't prepare it yourself, and you don't even know how to tell the cook to change it. Thinking about it, this kind of suffering is unavoidable for both men and women.

Generally, people who have lived in a foreign land for a while, if they have some leisure time, then researching cooking methods can be considered "a pleasure," right?

If we talk about cooking methods from a horizontal perspective—that is, in terms of type—the principles are nothing more than "steaming," "baking," time-consuming, roasting, mixing," seven characters. However, because "steaming," "baking," are time-consuming, and controlling the heat is not easy, ordinary cooking invariably falls within the scope of braising, boiling, frying, stir-frying, and mixing. Among these five, "mixing" is the easiest. Mixing is divided into cold mixing and hot mixing. Almost everyone knows how to mix cold dishes, such as "mixed jellyfish," "mixed cucumber," and "mixed tofu." Hot mixing is not common in Jiangsu and Zhejiang, but it is common in Yunnan, Guizhou, and Sichuan. Hot mixing seems like stir-frying, but to prevent the dishes from becoming too mushy, they are often pan-fried, and ingredients such as sauce, vinegar, and chili are mixed together. When boiling hot, they are poured from the pan into a bowl containing vegetables and stirred immediately with chopsticks to cook them. Examples include pickled cucumbers, oil-drenched cabbage, and oil-soaked tripe in Sichuan, Guizhou, and Yunnan cuisine, and also in Beijing cuisine. Pan-frying and oil-poaching are similar, but they are related to both "stir-frying" and "braising." For example, when cooking fish, except for steaming, you must first start by frying. By custom, in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and other provinces, mostly one side is fried until golden brown, and then it is braised with a sauce of five flavors (the method of braising West Lake Fish is simply not fried; the fresh fish is scaled, gutted, and washed, and then blanched in boiling water, and then a sauce is added. Therefore, it is very tender and fresh when eaten.) Further west, in provinces such as Hunan and Hubei, both sides must be fried until golden brown, while in Sichuan and Yunnan, people eat crispy-skinned fish that has been fried very thoroughly. As for salted fish, it is considered most delicious when pan-fried everywhere. When frying vegetables, the oil (mostly lard, but butter, goose fat, sesame oil, and vegetable oil can also be used) must be heated until extremely hot (if you sprinkle a little salt into the pan and hear a loud sound, it is extremely hot). At that time, put the fish and meat into the pan. In fact, the initial steps of "stir-frying" and "braising" are also the same. For "frying," more refined cooks use a frying pan. (Flat-bottomed pans are very popular nowadays because of the trend towards Europeanization. Small families often fry breaded fish, fried steak, ham and eggs, etc.) Roasting and grilling are not very different; it's just that meat is roasted directly in the fire with iron forks or tongs, iron chopsticks, etc., such as roast duck, roasted meat, crispy roasted pork, and roasted pork. Besides "roasting," there is another similar type of "smoking," such as smoked fish and smoked chicken. They must also go through the frying process beforehand, but the seasoning sauce must be applied to the entire surface of the fish or chicken in advance. There is very little frying time (use little oil to prevent sticking). After removing, put fennel, star anise, and other spices and pre-soaked dried tea leaves in the pan, and then put the fish and chicken on a special iron rack (crossed bamboo chopsticks will also work), supported on the spices, and burn the pot with a slow fire, so that the smoke from the spices rises up to smoke them.

Shanghai people always say "braise" side dishes in their everyday language, so "braising" is very popular in Shanghai; it's similar to how Suzhou people say "put it in the pot and steam it" all the time. This "braising" is called water-stir-frying in southwestern China, indicating that less oil is used and more water is used for help. Dishes such as stir-fried shredded pork with bean curd sheets, assorted seafood, oyster sauce tofu, and braised sliced radish with pork are different from stir-frying. In fact, dry-stir-frying and scorched-stir-frying, which are popular in Sichuan and Yunnan, are almost like frying. "Stir-frying" is as easy as "braising" in cooking. The so-called "water-stir-frying" "braising" cannot actually use less oil; however, a considerable amount of water can be added when mixing the five-flavor sauce. But everyone can perform magic tricks, and each has different skills. Just take the commonly eaten stir-fried shredded pork as an example; if you think about it carefully, everyone will find it interesting and marvel at the variety of stir-fried shredded pork. I can also take this opportunity to introduce a humorous story about stir-fried shredded pork to make everyone laugh.

This story has been passed down from the late Qing Dynasty, telling the story of a poor scholar in southern Fujian who, after the failure of Geng Jingzhong, one of the three feudatories, married a cook released from the Geng mansion as his wife. Hearing about the delicacies and strangely cooked dishes that Geng Jingzhong ate every day made the scholar's mouth water. He asked his wife to make two good dishes to satisfy his appetite. His wife said: I only managed one dish in the Geng mansion, which is "stir-fried shredded pork." I don't know how to do anything else. But this stir-fried shredded pork must be made with a strip of pork tenderloin taken from a whole pig. The scholar obeyed respectfully. He finally waited until the day of Confucius's birthday when sacrificial meat was distributed. He begged his colleagues at the school palace to get a strip of tenderloin and took it home to his wife. She cut it, mixed it with a five-flavor sauce, and stir-fried a bowl of shredded pork. Sure enough, it smelled wonderful. At this time, the scholar wanted to drink wine, so his wife went out to buy him wine. Who would have thought that when she returned, the scholar was lying in the kitchen, and the bowl of shredded pork had been eaten clean? She helped him up and asked what he was doing. The scholar mumbled incoherently. With great difficulty, she finally understood what he meant. It turned out that the scholar was so impatient because of the aroma of the stir-fried shredded pork that he began to chew it greedily on his own. When he finished eating everything in the bowl and chewing everything in his mouth, he unknowingly chewed and ate a section of his own tongue, so he fell to the ground in pain!

Now, let's talk about the vertical aspect of cooking methods—that is, the process from raw vegetables to cooked dishes. The first step is chopping board work. This work is dangerous. If you don't do it right, the big kitchen knife in your right hand can cut off your finger just like the tongue-chewing scholar. Therefore, when you buy fish, meat, and vegetables yourself or ask someone to buy them for you, you can tell the vegetable seller to cut them for you in advance. Whether it's shredded pork or fish cubes, it's all possible. The key is to mix the five-flavor sauce. When mixing, you can taste it yourself first and put a small bowl next to the pot to avoid the trouble of not knowing how to season it later. The next step is to rub the sliced ​​meat or shredded pork with a little cornstarch. When frying fish, you can mix it in the five-flavor sauce. After preparing outside the pot, start working inside the pot. Put oil, heat the oil, and sprinkle salt into the oil pan. When the oil is boiling, put the vegetables, meat, and fish into the oil pan. If the oil is very hot, the fish, meat, and vegetables that go in will definitely be cooked after flipping a few times (you don't have to worry about them not being cooked, so you burn them until they are old and tasteless). Then use a spoon to scoop them out and put them in a bowl; then separately fry the five-flavor sauce in the pot. Then, you can put the fish, meat, and vegetables back into the pot with the five-flavor sauce for a quick braise or stir-fry, or simply pour the five-flavor sauce over the bowl of fish, meat, and vegetables for a hot mix. In short, you can always distinguish which ones are easy to cook and which ones are not, and adjust their heat accordingly.

Nature gave people a nose and a tongue, both of which are extremely clever. By smelling and tasting, you can adapt to the situation and take advantage of it. Therefore, I think satisfying your appetite is not difficult. If you practice diligently, you will create some variations. The "color, aroma, taste, and presentation" are indispensable!

The color of the fire, the color of the vegetables, the color of the five-flavor sauce (many people don't use dark soy sauce and often use salt water to keep the color of the vegetables from turning black), and the color of the bowl. People who are skilled in cooking do pay attention to the "color" of the dishes. When they are brought to the table, if the color of the dishes is good and the aroma is complete, then the mouth and tongue will naturally match the appetite, and you will be satisfied. Moreover, cooking methods and knife skills are also closely related. Otherwise, if you use ingredients such as meat shredded like door planks, diced chicken like stone eggs, and vegetables chopped with random cuts, no matter how flavorful you make them, they will always be disgusting!

Knife skills are not difficult either. The sharper the kitchen knife, the better. The knife should be large, sharp, thin, and thick-backed. Whether you are cutting shredded pork, diced meat, sliced meat, or minced meat, you must first slice off the skin of a piece of raw meat; then slice and separate the fat and lean meat. (If you are braising red-braised pork, you should use streaky pork, and cut the fat, lean meat, and skin together. This is an exception.) Hold the knife in your right hand and hold the top of the square piece of meat with your left hand. Cut horizontally, slicing large pieces from right to left (you don't need to separate them). Then use the knife to cut from top to bottom. (At this time, you can separate three or five slices and stack them for cutting, which is easier for larger pieces.) First make strips of large shredded meat, then cut them open. Separate the fat and lean meat and place them in bowls separately. (When stir-frying shredded pork, put the fatty meat in the pot first, and the lean meat later, because the fatty meat has fat that can be rendered and is easier to eat when browned.) If you are cutting ingredients such as fish kidneys, belly, gizzards, and livers, the large slice work is the same. When you get to the small slices, you need to make patterns on the small slices (use a knife to carve net-shaped patterns or square patterns on the small slices). They will naturally curl into flower shapes when you put them in the pot.

Now, let's add a method for making a "Sichuan soup." Sichuan soup does not refer to Sichuan alone; however, this method is most common in Sichuan. Usually, everyone knows about sliced meat soup, but they often suffer from the soup being salty and cloudy, and the sliced meat is always tough. The characteristic of Sichuan soup is that it focuses on being light and fresh, clear and flavorful, and the sliced meat is tender and delicious. The addition of sliced fragrant mushrooms, sliced pickled mustard tuber, sliced loofah, and pea shoots makes the colors bright, green, and pleasing. For cooking, usually no colored soy sauce is used, only salt water and cornstarch are rubbed on the sliced ​​meat and placed in a small bowl separately; then cut fragrant mushrooms, pickled mustard tuber (must be washed and sliced), sliced loofah, or pea shoots and place them aside separately. When the water in the pot is about to boil, first put the pickled mustard tuber, fragrant mushrooms, and sliced loofah into it. After it boils, add the sliced ​​meat. The sliced ​​meat must be placed in a slotted spoon to allow it to float in the soup for about one or two minutes. As soon as it is cooked, scoop it out and put it in a large bowl, and then scoop the soup into the bowl (if it is the season for pea shoots, the pea shoots should also be handled like the sliced ​​meat, and cannot be put in the pot). While it is hot, sprinkle a little salt and a little pepper. When brought to the table, it is not only beautiful in color, but also very delicious in taste. Naturally, the people at the table will "love the Sichuan soup at first sight and eat it all up."

International Intelligence

Current Status of Gold Production in Various Countries

— Shi

Gold is the main currency of the capitalist world; although most countries in the world have abandoned the gold standard, the importance and role of gold in the capitalist world has not diminished as a result. We can see the domestic situation of a country from the amount of gold it holds and the flow of its surplus. Similarly, we can see the general international situation from information on the world's gold supply. What I am going to report on now is the recent situation of the world's gold supply.

First, let's talk about gold production. There was a sharp decrease after the last World War. The lowest production was in

Page 22

1922, when the total world gold production was 15.4 million ounces. After that, production showed an increasing trend, and by 1930, world gold production had increased to 16 million to 20 million ounces. However, this increase in production was uneven and inconsistent. For example, the production of the Rand gold mine in South Africa increased significantly at this time, and the production of the Soviet Union and Canada also increased slightly, but the production of the United States and Australia decreased.

After 1930, due to the development of the unprecedented Great Depression, the fall in prices, the devaluation of currency in the United Kingdom and the United States, and the high price of gold, gold production was greatly stimulated. Under this stimulus, the profits of gold production increased greatly, which continued to attract new investment in gold mines, promoted the expansion of old mines, and the development of new mines. First of all, the gold mines that had been abandoned in the western United States in the past were reopened at this time, and the development of new gold mines had developed to the southeast. The key is Canada, which at this time had reached areas far into the Arctic Circle for gold mining; in those places, gold mine owners used the latest gold mining methods and airplanes to extract and transport gold. At the same time, old mines in Australia, New Zealand, and Chile were also reopened. The old gold mine workers have continued to work, and the gold production has naturally returned to its former glory.

Among the increase in world gold production, it is worth paying special attention to the Soviet Union and South Africa. The former ranks first in the world in gold production, while the latter ranks second.

First, let's talk about the Soviet Union. In recent years, the number of people working in the gold mining industry in the Soviet Union has increased to 700,000. They use the latest type of dredges to replace the traditional manual washing method, which has greatly increased gold production in Siberia. Their gold mines are all mechanized. With the use of the latest machinery, the production of the Ural gold mines has recently increased greatly. Most of this gold is transported out by the Soviet government to purchase machinery and other needed items in order to strive for domestic construction.

As for the Union of South Africa, it is of course under British control. Therefore, its gold production is not only related to itself, but also related to the United Kingdom. First of all, with the United Kingdom's suspension of the gold standard, the South African gold pound also fell in price in December 1932, so the price of gold almost doubled. This result will of course promote the increase in gold production in South Africa. According to the current situation, it is estimated that the gold production in South Africa can increase to 15 million ounces.

Due to the rise in gold prices and the increase in gold production, South Africa's finances have naturally shown a good situation. In recent years, its treasury has had huge surpluses. The country's imports have also seen a significant increase. In 1932, they were 32 million pounds, but last year they increased to 75 million pounds; they more than doubled in three years. What do these facts indicate? In a word, it indicates the intensification of British imperialism's exploitation of the South African people and the active plunder of South African gold.

Now, we can also cite the following figures to more concretely show the recent production overview of the world's major gold producing areas—

Recent World Gold Production (unit: million old US dollars)

From this, it can be seen that world gold production has generally increased in recent years; among them, the increase in the Soviet Union and Canada is particularly obvious. As for the gold production for this year, there are of course no overall statistics yet, but judging from the situation in the past few months, it is still continuing to increase. According to a survey, world gold production in January-February of this year was 5.2 million ounces, an increase of about 800,000 ounces compared to the same period last year. Among them, the production of the Union of South Africa, Canada, and the United States was 100,000 ounces more than the same period last year. At the same time, the Soviet Union, which ranks second in the world, has recently announced a gold production increase plan. According to this plan, the Soviet Union will produce more than 10 million ounces of gold this year; this is more than doubled compared to last year. In this way, what can be imagined now is that the increase in world gold production this year will necessarily show a new record; according to general estimates, gold production this year can reach 33 million to 35 million ounces or more. However, what is worth noting here is that if this estimate becomes a reality, and at the same time the Soviet Union's plan is also realized, then it means that the Soviet Union's gold production will account for one-third of the world; and the speed of the increase in the Soviet Union's gold production will also be higher compared to the capitalist world.

The above is only the situation of increased gold production, which is only one aspect of the increased world gold supply. At the same time, on the other hand, due to the increase in gold production, the originally hidden gold continues to be released, so the world gold supply is even greater. What is worth paying special attention to in this process is that before the Great Depression, India and other Oriental countries were traditional gold hoarding countries, and they absorbed about two-thirds of the world's gold production every year at that time. However, after the panic, India and other countries became sellers of gold. For example, India has exported 180 million pounds (900 million US dollars) of gold in the past four years alone; if we add the gold flowing out of China and British Malaya, then the total amount of hidden gold released from the Far East will be over 1 billion pounds.

However, where did such a large amount of gold production and re-released hidden gold flow to? The first is in the gold scramble between imperialist countries, and countries such as the United States and France have obtained large amounts of gold reserves. The second is that due to the development of the world crisis, the rich in European countries are striving to buy gold at home and abroad for storage, which has also absorbed a large amount of cash. For example, last year, of the total world gold supply of 1.2 billion US dollars, about 700 million US dollars were added to the currency gold and craft expenses of central banks in various countries, and the other 500 million US dollars of gold were absorbed by individuals; these individuals are mainly the wealthy in Europe and the United States. According to a survey, the situation of private gold hoarding has been developing this year, and so far, the amount of gold being hoarded is probably more than 1 billion US dollars.

The increase in gold supply could have promoted the rise in prices, but in fact prices did not rise as expected. This is because the gold standard has not been restored in various countries. They are using exchange rate wars to lower prices in order to dump goods; and the existing gold has not been taken out for circulation. It has already been declared separate from the standard currency. As for the increase in gold supply, various countries are still not stopping the gold scramble, and individuals are still hoarding gold, which is of course a manifestation of the war crisis.

Wages of Workers in the Puppet State

— Translated by Bo

Workers in "Manchukuo" can be roughly divided into three types: Chinese, Japanese, and Korean, among which Chinese account for more than 95% of the total. According to statistics from the South Manchuria Railway Company, the wages earned by Chinese workers employed in the company's repair factories are only equal to a quarter of the wages earned by Japanese workers in the same factory. In addition, the situation is similar in all other factories in "Manchukuo."

In recent years, due to the social recession, wages in "Manchukuo," whether for Chinese workers or Japanese workers, have generally decreased, but the wages of Chinese workers have been reduced more. For example, from April 1928 to February 1933, the wages of Chinese workers in the Fushun coal mine were reduced by 11.3%, while the wages of Japanese workers were only reduced by 7.8%.

As for Chinese agricultural workers in "Manchukuo," their wages have been greatly reduced - in some cases, they have been reduced by half.

In addition, there are also those who do not receive any wages at all, or even do not receive wages at all. Needless to say, their lives are more difficult than those of other workers.

One more thing to pay attention to is that you must not only pat the throat, but also pat the back of the neck at the same time, because the back of the neck is more important and obvious than the throat.
